  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2a7ae105-7b9e-44e2-aadf-f9b898cfaac5'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer14656679995273917271">Cheerleader Isobel Lanley is horrified when she is paired with Varen Nethers for an English project, which is due—so unfair—on the day of the rival game.   <span id="freeText14656679995273917271" style="display:none">Cheerleader Isobel Lanley is horrified when she is paired with Varen Nethers for an English project, which is due—so unfair—on the day of the rival game. Cold and aloof, sardonic and sharp-tongued, Varen makes it clear he’d rather not have anything to do with her either. But when Isobel discovers strange writing in his journal, she can’t help but give this enigmatic boy with the piercing eyes another look. <br /><br />Soon, Isobel finds herself making excuses to be with Varen. Steadily pulled away from her friends and her possessive boyfriend, Isobel ventures deeper and deeper into the dream world Varen has created through the pages of his notebook, a realm where the terrifying stories of Edgar Allan Poe come to life. <br /><br />As her world begins to unravel around her, Isobel discovers that dreams, like words, hold more power than she ever imagined, and that the most frightening realities are those of the mind. Now she must find a way to reach Varen before he is consumed by the shadows of his own nightmares. <br /><br /><b>His life depends on it.</b></span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    They did get a "happily ever after" ending. Of course, Varen had to die before it could happen but ultimately they are together; he's back in the real<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    They did get a "happily ever after" ending. Of course, Varen had to die before it could happen but ultimately they are together; he's back in the real world again. At least, that's what was suggested at the end of Oblivion when Isobel's dad said she could invite Varen over for dinner or whatever. I was kind of confused at the ending too, but then he said that and I was relieved. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

Yes! Nevermore is a trilogy. The order of the books are: Nevermore, Enshadowed, and Oblivion, which was just released on July 28th. :)

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115634941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10007209521877889138">It's been a while since a YA paranormal truly blew me away. But this book did. It actually made me stay up until 3 a.m. although I had to get up at seven the next morning (and yes, I regretted this afterwards).<br/><br/>Despite the praise it got from a lot of friends here on GoodReads, I tried to keep my expectations low before starting it. Books in this genre have disappointed me many times before. After reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3975774.Evermore__The_Immortals___1_' title='Evermore (The Immortals, #1) by Alyson Noel' rel='nofollow noopener'>Evermore</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2722413.Evernight__Evernight___1_' title='Evernight (Evernight, #1) by Claudia Gray' rel='nofollow noopener'>Evernight</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6304335.Beautiful_Creatures__Caster_Chronicles___1_' title='Beautiful Creatures (Caster Chronicles, #1) by Kami Garcia' rel='nofollow noopener'>Beautiful Creatures</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30183.Marked__House_of_Night___1_' title='Marked (House of Night, #1) by P.C. Cast' rel='nofollow noopener'>Marked</a> and the like, I’ve become careful and a bit </span>
  <span id="freeText10007209521877889138" style="display:none">It's been a while since a YA paranormal truly blew me away. But this book did. It actually made me stay up until 3 a.m. although I had to get up at seven the next morning (and yes, I regretted this afterwards).<br /><br />Despite the praise it got from a lot of friends here on GoodReads, I tried to keep my expectations low before starting it. Books in this genre have disappointed me many times before. After reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3975774.Evermore__The_Immortals___1_" title="Evermore (The Immortals, #1) by Alyson Noel" rel="nofollow noopener">Evermore</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2722413.Evernight__Evernight___1_" title="Evernight (Evernight, #1) by Claudia Gray" rel="nofollow noopener">Evernight</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6304335.Beautiful_Creatures__Caster_Chronicles___1_" title="Beautiful Creatures (Caster Chronicles, #1) by Kami Garcia" rel="nofollow noopener">Beautiful Creatures</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30183.Marked__House_of_Night___1_" title="Marked (House of Night, #1) by P.C. Cast" rel="nofollow noopener">Marked</a> and the like, I’ve become careful and a bit picky and stayed away from quite a few novels that received high ratings.<br /><br />But this one definitely deserved the praise. I found the paranormal aspect fascinating and original. I have never read anything by Poe nor do I know much about his life (and death, for that matter), but Creagh has succeeded in raising my interest and got me thinking about picking up some of his work. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I also googled the 'Poe Toaster' and found out that he didn't show this year! I really hope that's not what happens in the novel. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I found it amazing how she interwove elements from Poe's life and stories with the mysteries surrounding his demise and developed an eerie and scary, but at the same time awe-inspiring world around them.<br /><br />But to be honest: most of all, this story lives on the interaction between its two main characters. And I loved those characters. Especially Varen. Yes, I think I might even have a little literary crush on him. He is a refreshing change from all those brooding and mysterious heroes with their sometimes stalker-like obsessions towards the heroine. He isn't a jerk because hey, he’s mysterious and hot and therefore can afford it. <br />His 'mysteriousness' (if you want to call it so) comes mostly from the fact that he keeps to himself and stays within his small group of friends and – of course – from his outer appearance that clearly says: stay away from me. But once he and Isobel get to know each other better, you can actually see that there is way more to him than his looks and that he isn't as hostile as he pretends to be. I really liked his subtle sense of humour and how you could see that he cared for Isobel without him making grand gestures and declaring his undying love. (Thanks a lot for the lack of declarations of love after knowing each other for one day, I really appreciated it!)<br /><br />That leads me to Isobel. As the story is told from her point of view, I was exceptionally glad that she isn't one of those whiny and – let’s be honest – stupid heroines I've encountered in the books mentioned above. She might not make the wisest decisions at certain points in the story (seriously, what makes a sensible 16-year-old take the way home through a deserted park at night?), but those moments are scarce and don't make her less likable. I liked that she doesn't give in to peer pressure although it might cost her the place among the popular crowd and how she doesn't hold back her fury when she feels treated the wrong way.<br /><br />Her so-called 'friends' behave horribly, but Creagh manages to include something in them that doesn't make them all loathsome and therefore they aren't painted strictly in black and white.<br /><br />Also great: for a change, the protagonist's family plays an important role in the novel. Isobel's parents are strict and some of their decisions seem rather harsh, but they definitely care a lot for her daughter and her problems. I loved the interactions between the family members: how her little brother seems to care about nothing much expect his video games but is always there to cover for her when she is in trouble, and especially how her dad doesn't hesitate to make a complete fool out of himself in front of a horde of teenagers to help Isobel with her class project.<br /> <br />So, in fact, my only complaint here is: Why does it end on such a mean cliffhanger? The story ended way too apruptly, and hadn't I loved the book so much, I might have been less forgiving about that. (Cliffhangers always make me think I'm tortured on purpose and lured into wanting to buy the next book. No bait necessary here, folks!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="10007209521877889138" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1594906-kim?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78453978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1541559724208718877">This review is difficult to write because I usually don't have that much to say about books I love. It's mostly facial expressions, gestures and noises when I try to explain why I like something. Oh and it will look like this was written by a 17-year old, not a 27-year old. And I'm sorry, but I just can't help myself. I even wish I could write this review in purple ink, <i>that's</i> how much I'm into this book. And Varen. ♥<br/><br/>If I ever had to describe the kind of guy I desperately want then I think Varen</span>
  <span id="freeText1541559724208718877" style="display:none">This review is difficult to write because I usually don't have that much to say about books I love. It's mostly facial expressions, gestures and noises when I try to explain why I like something. Oh and it will look like this was written by a 17-year old, not a 27-year old. And I'm sorry, but I just can't help myself. I even wish I could write this review in purple ink, <i>that's</i> how much I'm into this book. And Varen. ♥<br /><br />If I ever had to describe the kind of guy I desperately want then I think Varen comes closer than anybody else. (minus the eyeliner, I just can't imagine it looks hot on any guy, just emo). You wouldn't believe how much I'm crushing on him. Oh don't give me that look, half the planet swoons over a dead guy whose genitals sparkle in the sunlight, so don't act like this is weird.<br /><br />So, meet Isobel, your typical cheerleader who lives up to every stereotype that comes with being a girl who waves pom poms around in a short skirt. Meet Varen, your typical... Um... I dunno. Nothing I say will make him look good. So I'll stick with saying he's smart, witty, funny, deep, sardonic and not to mention interesting.<br /><br />They are forced to work together on a school paper on Poe and I don't think I need to make clear how much both of them are looking forward to working with each other. To make matters even worse: It doesn't go smooth to begin with and Isobel's overprotective (I just say he's jealous and insecure as hell) boyfriend decides to make Varen's life miserable because he wrote his number on Isobel's hand in class.<br /><br />Isobel didn't want Brad to know because he would overreact but her 'friend' Nikki, who I didn't like from the moment I met her, decided to tell anyway. There was a part about how badly she wanted to tell Brad. I could have punched her in the face.<br /><br />But waring Varen didn't seem to be enough for Brad and the rest of his gang of idiots. They mess up the ice cream parlor (of all the places a guy like Varen could work...), much to my, and Isobel's disgust.<br /><br />I won't give away too much of the story, because I want all of you to read this beautiful book but I enjoyed reading this so much.<br /><br />The pink ribbon on the back... The raven... And the kiss. <i>That</i> kiss. I read those lines 50 times already and thinking about them still gives me chills. I'm in love!<br /><br />I can't wait to get my hands on the sequel.</span>

<div id="review_156190200" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156190200" />
    <a title="Limonessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa"><img alt="Limonessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424025988p2/4147373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156190200?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Limonessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Limonessa" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa">Limonessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=paranormal-ya">paranormal-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=swoooooon">swoooooon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156190200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10717890825123714606">They say not to judge a book by its cover. That appearances are deceitful.<br/><br/>I say this time you should not judge the book by how it starts off. At first, it very much looks like your garden-variety paranormal YA: jocks, cheerleaders, cliques, mean girls, emo-goths, star crossed lovers, you get the gist. There were a couple of scenes at the beginning where I thought I was probably going to ditch it if it went on like it was. <br/>But it didn't.<br/>First of all, you should be aware that underneath the shallo</span>
  <span id="freeText10717890825123714606" style="display:none">They say not to judge a book by its cover. That appearances are deceitful.<br /><br />I say this time you should not judge the book by how it starts off. At first, it very much looks like your garden-variety paranormal YA: jocks, cheerleaders, cliques, mean girls, emo-goths, star crossed lovers, you get the gist. There were a couple of scenes at the beginning where I thought I was probably going to ditch it if it went on like it was. <br />But it didn't.<br />First of all, you should be aware that underneath the shallow, clichéd appearance, this book is very dark and oneiric. I don't know if you're familiar with the work of Edgar Allan Poe, but the story is based and heavily influenced by several of his writings, such as <i>The Raven</i>, <i>The Masque of Red Death</i> and <i>Ligeia</i>, among others. Parts of his biography, especially concerning the mysterious circumstances of his death, are also a fundamental part of the plot. <br /><br />The story starts, quite predictably, with Isobel - blonde, cheerleader, girlfriend of THE football player of the school - getting paired up for an English project with Varen - goth guy, aloof, antisocial, with a mean girlfriend but magnetically irresistible. Despite a rocky start, as Isobel's feelings for Varen change and grow into something even she is reluctant to accept, strange things start to happen. Isobel gets chased by voices, she starts hallucinating, supposedly. <br />Who is causing all this? The key seems to be a book of the works of Edgar Allan Poe that Varen has given to her her for the project and that appears to have a life of its own. <br /><br />Nevermore came as a surprise to me, really. <br />Despite glowing reviews (and some non-glowing), I wasn't expecting much from it. This seemed to be confirmed in the first few chapters, when all the clichés made their entrance, and the mean girls theme put me in eye-rolling mode. <br />BUT. As the Raven theme crept more and more into the story and the clichés were left behind, the plot turned into something truly and incredibly original. I am sorry for those readers who dropped the book before getting to that part because, really, they missed out on something good. <br />The second part, which takes place in a sort of dreamland, a story inside the stories, was truly engaging and fascinating for me. The star-crossed lovers got separated, grotesque figures started appearing, Isobel became a dark Alice in Wonderland, right after she fell into the hole. <br />I'll admit: not everybody will like it. It can be confusing at times and many people won't like the romance being set aside to see other characters steal the scene with their bloody razor teeth. Me, I loved it. I love when a book manages to surprise and frankly, this did it successfully. <br /><br />As far as I am concerned, a success. I can't wait to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9239571._Enshadowed__Nevermore___2_" title=" Enshadowed (Nevermore, #2) by Kelly Creagh" rel="nofollow noopener">Enshadowed</a> when it comes out in August, 2012. <br /><br />I'm taking away one star for the name Varen.<br />First of all, WHY the lame anagram?<br />Second, unfortunately everytime I read the name, <a href="http://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Varenne.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> was the image I had in my mind. Ops.<br /><br />For this review and more, go to <a href="http://thenocturnallibrary.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Nocturnal Library</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10717890825123714606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_77595563" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77595563" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496094866p2/1310688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77595563?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=signed-books">signed-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77595563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6048731384490707765">I loved this book. <br/><br/>I wanted to love this book, but I was a little apprehensive. I mean... the goth boy and the cheerleader. Haven't I read this story before.... No, Kristi, you have not read a story quite like this one before.<br/><br/>In addition to loving the pages in this book I also love this cover. I wish that B&N hadn't had a little hissy fit and the publisher would have been able to keep Varen's lip ring.... it was so much hotter with the lip ring. But I still love the cover regardless.<br/><br/>The characte</span>
  <span id="freeText6048731384490707765" style="display:none">I loved this book. <br /><br />I wanted to love this book, but I was a little apprehensive. I mean... the goth boy and the cheerleader. Haven't I read this story before.... No, Kristi, you have not read a story quite like this one before.<br /><br />In addition to loving the pages in this book I also love this cover. I wish that B&amp;N hadn't had a little hissy fit and the publisher would have been able to keep Varen's lip ring.... it was so much hotter with the lip ring. But I still love the cover regardless.<br /><br />The characters are what made this novel for me. Isobel &amp; Varen were extremely well written, well fleshed out characters. They had a depth to them, especially Varen, I haven't witnessed that sort of depth in a while. I find that I often complain about friendships between characters... especially when the main character continues to stay in a toxic friendship. I loved Isobel for standing up for herself and not becoming a doormat for her not so great friends. Their falling out while I thought it was a little extreme at times, worked rather nicely. I have to say that I Isobel's new friends were much more appealing.<br /><br />I loved the references to the Poe.... the small insights to his life, factual and fictionalized. I actually had to go out and buy the complete works of Edgar Allan Poe after reading the novel. I forgot how much I enjoyed his twisted story that I had read in high school.... The Fall of the House of Usher, The Tell-Tale Heart, The Raven.... I'm looking forward to reading more.<br /><br />As much as I loved the story, I do have to say that I was a little confused at times durning the last quarter of the novel... when Isobel is in the 'dream' world. Some of the passages required a re-reading to understand exactly what was going on, and often times, I still wasn't 100% sure. But other than that, I loved the developing relationship between Isobel and Raven.... and Isobel and Gwen. How cool was Gwen. She's the best friend I always wanted in high school.<br /><br />Nevermore is a tale of a dark romance with a wickedly twisted Poe inspiration.<br /><br />You will definitely want to read this awesomeness for yourself. I can't wait to read book two. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6048731384490707765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_157142869" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/157142869" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1489224-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338449051p2/1489224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157142869?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/1489224-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1489224-lisa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1489224-lisa?shelf=paranormal-romance-urban-fantasy">paranormal-romance-urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1489224-lisa?shelf=debbie-downer">debbie-downer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157142869" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1446775493305182649">When I picked up <i>Nevermore</i> I was expecting to like it. So many of my Goodreads friends rated it highly as did the overall Goodreads community. Unfortunately after finishing the novel I'm sorry to say that it was barely a two star read for me.<br/><br/><i>Nevermore</i> tells the story of Isobel Lanely, a popular blonde cheerleader, who is partnered with super goth, Varen Nethers, for an English project about Edgar Allen Poe. This pairing, which was chosen by the teacher, causes outrage among Isobel's friends. Her</span>
  <span id="freeText1446775493305182649" style="display:none">When I picked up <i>Nevermore</i> I was expecting to like it. So many of my Goodreads friends rated it highly as did the overall Goodreads community. Unfortunately after finishing the novel I'm sorry to say that it was barely a two star read for me.<br /><br /><i>Nevermore</i> tells the story of Isobel Lanely, a popular blonde cheerleader, who is partnered with super goth, Varen Nethers, for an English project about Edgar Allen Poe. This pairing, which was chosen by the teacher, causes outrage among Isobel's friends. Her quarterback boyfriend, Brad, is so enraged at Varen for daring to be partnered with Isobel against his will that he starts harassing him. And this is where <i>Nevermore</i> lost me, during the very first chapter.<br /><br />I found the characters and plot to be so completely unbelievable that I could never really get into the story. I never understood what was so scandalous about Isobel and Varen being partners for a class assignment. Why would this cause gossip among Isobel's friends, or cause her boyfriend to go ballistic? It makes absolutely no sense.<br /><br />Brad is a cartoonish villain. There is no depth to his character. He is a jerk, plain and simple. Isobel is shown to be disgusted by him from the very beginning, which begs the question of why she was with him in the first place. Brad has no redeeming qualities, and Isobel is shown to be a nice girl, who lacks the kind of insecurities that would drive her to date someone like Brad. The fact that he's a football player and she's a cheerleader does not adequately explain their relationship.<br /><br />The other secondary characters also lack depth and are mainly used as plot devices. Alyssa is your cliché bitchy cheerleader with platinum blonde hair. Her sole purpose in this novel is to be mean to Isobel and side with Brad. Nikki's purpose in the novel is a mystery. She and Alyssa could easily have been combined into one character and it wouldn't have changed anything. Varen's sort-of girlfriend, Lacy, also served no purpose and could easily have been removed altogether.<br /><br />Gwen is slightly better developed in that she doesn't fit any cliché and occasionally has a backbone, but she is there only as a plot device. Whenever Isobel needs someone to sit with, someone to talk to, or a ride, Gwen shows up. Gwen's life revolves around Isobel and Isobel does nothing but use Gwen. Even in the end when Gwen confronts Isobel about avoiding her, Isobel only reaches out to her because she needs her help with Varen.<br /><br />Isobel's family doesn't fair much better. Her brother Danny, like Gwen, serves only as a plot device. Her father seems mostly to be another foil for her relationship with Varen. At one point he refuses to let her leave the house to work on the class project with him even though her grade depends on it. He also likes Brad and supports him over his own daughter for some inexplicable reason. Her mother is completely forgettable.<br /><br />I also found myself unimpressed with either Isobel or Varen. Isobel's actions and decisions are often nonsensical like dating Brad, not telling Varen about Reynolds, and sneaking out to do homework, so I never could see her as a real person. Varen showed promise, but his character wasn't fleshed out enough to be truly compelling to me. I agree with other reviewers that if the novel had been written from his perspective it would have been a much more interesting read.<br /><br />Another major problem I had with the story was that I did not buy the romance. Isobel is drawn to Varen from the beginning, before she learns that there's more to him than just being a goth, and by the end of the novel, which takes place over the course of a month, she's willing to die for him and risk the lives of her friends and family for him. This was especially unbelievable given that he was a moody jerk towards her for a large chunk of that month. That said, I liked that the love interest didn't follow the typical YA cliché of being super beautiful and talented, and the relationship, while unbelievable, wasn't abusive or controlling. <br /><br />My feelings about the writing are mixed. While I enjoyed Creagh's writing style in terms of her sentence structure, word choice, and imagery, there was too much description. Very little is left to the reader's imagination and a lot of it was unnecessary. I felt like it ended up bogging down the story. Creagh frequently interrupts action scenes with description, slowing them down, making the story hard to follow at times.<br /><br />I do give Creagh credit for being original in terms of her mythology. It was very creative to spin a mythology around the life and works of Edgar Allen Poe. Creagh's love for Poe's works is evident in the text, and the novel appears to be well researched, though admittedly I am not the best judge since I am no expert on Poe.<br /><br />I wish I could say that I enjoyed this book more, but it wasn't my cup of tea. To each their own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1446775493305182649" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1734773745023926133"><i>
  <b>This. Book.</b>
</i> <br/><a href='http://photobucket.com/images/crying%20gifs' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380351907ra/705449.gif' alt='crying Pictures, Images and Photos' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Is nothing like I've ever read before. Sure it starts out in a school, like most cliche books. But then it gets creepy and wicked. And considering as how it's based on Edgar Allan Poe's works...it doesn't surprise me. It <i>excites</i> me. :3 Also, it makes me want to read some of his pieces. And I have <i>The Complete Tales and Poems of Edgar Allan Poe</i> myself, so...*hugs it tightly to my chest*<br/><br/>I really <s>liked</s> <i>loved</i> this book because it keeps me guessing on what will happen, and what/wh</span>
  <span id="freeText1734773745023926133" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>This. Book.</b>
</i> <br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/crying%20gifs" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380351907ra/705449.gif" alt="crying Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Is nothing like I've ever read before. Sure it starts out in a school, like most cliche books. But then it gets creepy and wicked. And considering as how it's based on Edgar Allan Poe's works...it doesn't surprise me. It <i>excites</i> me. :3 Also, it makes me want to read some of his pieces. And I have <i>The Complete Tales and Poems of Edgar Allan Poe</i> myself, so...*hugs it tightly to my chest*<br><br>I really <s>liked</s> <i>loved</i> this book because it keeps me guessing on what will happen, and what/who people are. Usually, when I read books, I sometimes see stuff coming, or be like, "<i>Oh! I know who's been sneaking around on so-and-so's wife.</i>" That's rhetorically speaking, just so you know. :P But this didn't happen with <i>Nevermore</i>. It actually made me gasp in a few scenes. And I freaking enjoyed the hell out of it.<br><br>Varen. Oh, Varen. How I love thee. You caught my eye right off the bat. And the thing is, this is related to my previous statement, is that I <i>could not</i>, for the life of me, figure out what the fuck he was. And I still don't know. If someone knows, or has an idea, please enlighten me. D: Because it's driving me crazy!<br> <br>And can I just say that I hate Brad, Nikki, Alyssa, and Mark? Like, I know Nikki apologized, and you'd think it would be for all four of them.. But I didn't really get that vibe. So I still hate them all, not caring either. :D I don't care if <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Brad broke his leg, and ventured off into the unknown land of Varen's mind. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> He's still a prick. All in all, this was a <i>
  <b>epic</b>
</i> book. And I can't wait until the next one. :D *rips hair out in the process*</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_83531766" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83531766" />
    <a title="Alexa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1894085-alexa"><img alt="Alexa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393730599p2/1894085.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83531766?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexa" href="/user/show/1894085-alexa">Alexa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=to-reread">to-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=2010-reads">2010-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=tour">tour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=exceeded-expectations">exceeded-expectations</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83531766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18068198027709021633"><br/>My review can also be found on my blog <a href='http://collections-books.blogspot.com/2010/08/review-nevermore-by-kelly-creagh.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Collections</a>.<br/><br/>O.M.G.<br/><br/>That was my reaction, anyway, to the majority of the book. Maybe I had such a strong reaction because I started the book not realizing this was a paranormal. Yes, I read the summary, but obviously it went over my head. This is what I assumed it would be about: <i>The goth boy, Varen, would have some mental issues (like schizophrenia), and the popular cheerleader girl, Isobel, will fall in love with him and find help for him. And they would al</i></span>
  <span id="freeText18068198027709021633" style="display:none"><br />My review can also be found on my blog <a href="http://collections-books.blogspot.com/2010/08/review-nevermore-by-kelly-creagh.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Collections</a>.<br /><br />O.M.G.<br /><br />That was my reaction, anyway, to the majority of the book. Maybe I had such a strong reaction because I started the book not realizing this was a paranormal. Yes, I read the summary, but obviously it went over my head. This is what I assumed it would be about: <i>The goth boy, Varen, would have some mental issues (like schizophrenia), and the popular cheerleader girl, Isobel, will fall in love with him and find help for him. And they would all live happily ever after.</i><br /><br />I mean, yeah, they are opposites, and they do fall in love, but it was not that simple. It's dark and creepy and eerie. A horror paranormal. (Of course, I should have realized that with Edgar Allan Poe involved). Which made it very exciting for me because I had no idea what would happen next and how this would end.<br /><br />There were some other things I just did not notice before I read the book. Like the length. It is 500+ pages! Which is not a bad thing because Isobel &amp; Varen's relationship and everything in the story isn't rushed. And at the same time, it didn't feel slow. I felt like something interesting was always happening. And I really liked Kelly Creagh's writing. It was like watching a movie.<br /><br />Now for the other detail I missed. Actually, I just didn't know. I'm pretty sure not much people know, so let me tell you.<br />This is going to be a series. A trilogy, apparently.<br />I know! That was really surpring to me. You would think that a book this long would have everything resolved by the end, but nope, not the case. I will not spoil the ending, but let me just say that when I read the last line in the book, I was thinking, <i>There should be sequel. There has to be a sequel. There NEEDS to be a sequel. o_o</i><br /><br />So I haven't revealed much about the story. Well, I don't want to repeat the summary, so I will say this: I was very impressed with the book. I thought the story was really unique and original. Isobel and Varen were great and likeable characters. I wanted to hug Varen! I was proud of Isobel (she deserves a hug too), because she worked so hard to save Varen. Basically, it all goes down October 31. Halloween. But it's not over. Just wait till January 19, the day of Poe's birth.<br /><br />Seriously can't wait! &gt;.&lt;</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_97022566" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97022566" />
    <a title="Amelia, free market Puritan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan"><img alt="Amelia, free market Puritan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508223427p2/1852293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97022566?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amelia, free market Puritan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amelia, free market Puritan" href="/user/show/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan">Amelia, free market Puritan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=ya-kids-teen">ya-kids-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=memorable-characters">memorable-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=point-of-view-girl">point-of-view-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=loveable-love-story">loveable-love-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=series-books">series-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=the-favorites">the-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97022566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18150244447758665706">What I want you to know about this book: Of all the 2010 releases I've read this year, NEVERMORE ties with <i>Tyger Tyger</i> as my favorite. The only drawback to it is the length of time we have to wait for the second installment! So just be prepared to take up chewing your nails, pacing, and crawling up the walls once you finish this...<br/><br/>The basic setup for the story - loner, reclusive goth boy and Miss Peppy cheerleader are paired for an English project - just really doesn't begin to cover this epic 5</span>
  <span id="freeText18150244447758665706" style="display:none">What I want you to know about this book: Of all the 2010 releases I've read this year, NEVERMORE ties with <i>Tyger Tyger</i> as my favorite. The only drawback to it is the length of time we have to wait for the second installment! So just be prepared to take up chewing your nails, pacing, and crawling up the walls once you finish this...<br /><br />The basic setup for the story - loner, reclusive goth boy and Miss Peppy cheerleader are paired for an English project - just really doesn't begin to cover this epic 500+ page saga. I was so curious as to how the author would incorporate Edgar Allan Poe and his works into a modern high school drama setting. But boy howdy, she did. I saw so many Poe references brilliantly and cleverly inserted into the story, and that made reading so very, very enjoyable. Watch for scenes from <i>Cask of Amontillado</i>, a glass-eyed dude bearing strong resemblance to the old man from <i>The Tell Tale Heart</i>, a raven or two, and more! Also, one of the chapter titles is called "Ulalume," which is one of my all-time favorite poems. What I'm trying to say is that this book doesn't just name-drop Poe a few times or make vague, random references to the poet or his works. Instead, Kelly blends Poe's masterpieces with her own incredible imagination to create an original, engaging and highly addictive story.<br />The characters, too, were so amazing. First off, the main character, Isobel, is not really what you'd expect: she is a cheerleader, but instead of being an overly-cheerful, hyperactive airhead, she actually is really smart, witty, and well-spoken. Varen, too, is not quite what you'd expect either. He was definitely likable, but his cold and aloof personality made him very peculiar - he was actually kind of the mean one in the relationship. While maintaining a steady pace throughout, the first 400 pages gave me a chance to really see the characters interact and get a good understanding for them. Everybody, this is how to portray well-rounded, dynamic characters. And at the same time, Creagh subtly built up the suspense: something's not quite right with Varen, and his peculiar "gift" turns out to be quite a curse. The last 100 pages *BAM* accelerate you into a fantastical-but-creepy dreamworld that Poe himself would probably enjoy. And oh, the ending! How it will make you desperate for the next installment!<br /><br />Quick say: Everybody, NEVERMORE is an exceptional debut by an amazingly gifted author. You will not want to pass this up. I have a new favorite! And Kelly Creagh has definitely set the standard and raised the bar for exceptional Young Adult paranormal fiction. THIS is what creativity and originality looks like. THIS BOOK RIGHT HERE!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18150244447758665706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123866202?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123866202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8530077832316308441"><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kelly-creagh/nevermore-review.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339972i/696537.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>First read in September 2010:</b><br/>Even though I am not usually into this kind of paranormal stories, and the goth things are not my type either, Nevermore had something really special that kept me reading from the first page to the last one (and wanting for more). <br/><br/>The story seems simple in the beginning: Isobel is paired with Varen in an English project and, as different as they are (she - a cheerleader, he - a strange goth boy), they get to know each other better and slowly fell in love one for </span>
  <span id="freeText8530077832316308441" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kelly-creagh/nevermore-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339972i/696537.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>First read in September 2010:</b><br>Even though I am not usually into this kind of paranormal stories, and the goth things are not my type either, Nevermore had something really special that kept me reading from the first page to the last one (and wanting for more). <br><br>The story seems simple in the beginning: Isobel is paired with Varen in an English project and, as different as they are (she - a cheerleader, he - a strange goth boy), they get to know each other better and slowly fell in love one for the other. <br>NOTE: If you think that this is the typical american story, then guess again because the book is anything but typical, and it is not as predictable as you might think. <br><br>What I liked the most about this book was the way the author handled the relationship between all the characters (Isobel and Varen, Isobel and her (ex)boyfriend, Isobel and Gwen, Isobel and her (ex)friends, etc.) and how the action took place step by step. <br><br>In this book, as long as it is, K.C. took her time for all little details as the story unfolded, and the characters started to grow on me slowly, making me feel like a part of the book, feeling like it was my own journey and not Isobel's only. At the same time, it never felt slow because there was always something interesting about to happen. <br><br>Another thing I love about this book is the fact that it fells 'real' - the connection between main characters, the dialogue, the action, even the paranormal elements were made to feel real, possible. Also the incorporation of poetry, of Poe was great (amazingly well done) and it played such an important role into the story.<br><br>The writing was impeccable, the plot complex with so many turnarounds, the characters are unique (and smart), the suspense makes you keep reading almost without breathing. I just can't wait for the second one to come out :)<br><br>__<br><br> <b>Re-read it in July 2012</b> and still loved it! <br>(some additional thought to come soon)<br><br>__<br><br>PS: I definitely have to say one more thing: the English project was NOT just a way to start the story, but it turned to be a great moment in the book too.. just wait for it! <br><br>See, this is what i like about this author, nothing is there just to fill in the blanks, everything has a reason in this book, and after reading this novel I got the feeling that I need to read it one more time.<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kelly-creagh/nevermore-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380313075i/688704.jpg" alt="" width="361" height="116" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>This review can be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kelly-creagh/nevermore-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a></i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122096849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2577130281797480719">I . LOVED. IT. <br/><br/>No seriously, I am like obsessed with this book. So, let’s see, it’s around 543 pages, I started this last night around 6:30 PM and it’s 11:47 AM the next day. I have never read a book this thick THAT fast. I am crazy, but holy shit that was a great ride. Woot!<br/><br/>This isn’t going to be a full-front in detail review, because it would just be rants of love. But this is the reason I truly adore the story: It’s so original. Oh, and yeah, Varen.<br/> <br/>I think you-- yes you reading this-- unders</span>
  <span id="freeText2577130281797480719" style="display:none">I . LOVED. IT. <br /><br />No seriously, I am like obsessed with this book. So, let’s see, it’s around 543 pages, I started this last night around 6:30 PM and it’s 11:47 AM the next day. I have never read a book this thick THAT fast. I am crazy, but holy shit that was a great ride. Woot!<br /><br />This isn’t going to be a full-front in detail review, because it would just be rants of love. But this is the reason I truly adore the story: It’s so original. Oh, and yeah, Varen.<br /> <br />I think you-- yes you reading this-- understand that when I say I’m sick of the perfect boy that’s all beautiful, sparkles or glows in the dark (whatever's in right now I guess) etc etc, that you agree. Varen is the total opposite. Sure, I mean, he wasn't described as completely disgusting or anything, but the way he was described was just so uniquely done and….oh Varen I love you so much! Marry me!<br /><br />Basically, you need to go pick this book up right now. It has a dreamworld and everything, and awesome people. You know you want to read it. <br /><br />Throughout high school, I was obsessed with Poe. I took his poems and wrote my own versions, I love his utter creepiness, and how dark he is. So, this book really drove me into getting back into Poe, because I truly love him! <br /><br />This is one of those books I got so lost in that I wasn't worrying about page numbers or the length of the chapters, well actually I wanted them to be super long so I could get more of the story but you know what I mean. <br /><br />I am afraid to read another book, because I know it won't be nearly as good as this. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2577130281797480719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12501400341596402018">WHAAAAAT?!?!<br/><br/>I've been sucked in by this book for the last two days - ignoring my family and my life (yes, it was THAT GOOD) - only to come to the uber-shocking, frustrating, non-ending ending. So, as a result, I'm going to walk away from it and give it NO RATING until I can make peace with where things were left (because, I feel that the ending completely skews my opinion of the book as a whole).<br/><br/>And no, while I didn't expect a happily-ever-after ending or to have all the loose ends nicely tied u</span>
  <span id="freeText12501400341596402018" style="display:none">WHAAAAAT?!?!<br /><br />I've been sucked in by this book for the last two days - ignoring my family and my life (yes, it was THAT GOOD) - only to come to the uber-shocking, frustrating, non-ending ending. So, as a result, I'm going to walk away from it and give it NO RATING until I can make peace with where things were left (because, I feel that the ending completely skews my opinion of the book as a whole).<br /><br />And no, while I didn't expect a happily-ever-after ending or to have all the loose ends nicely tied up in a neat little bow, I do feel as if the rug was pulled out from under me unexpectedly. For the record, let me just say that Nevermore was gearing up to be a 4.5-star read, but the end just left me feeling cheated.<br /><br />Yeah, I get that the ending is a cliffy meant to leave me panting for the next book, but DAMN, that was just plain mean. I despise NON-ENDING endings.<br /><br />That said, would I recommend that you read it? Yes. Do I think you'll be surprised (if not mad) at the ending? Yes. <br /><br /><i>Okay, okay, this may be a mixed-message non-review review , but hell, I need to rant about this book somewhere. </i><br /><br /><br />OCTOBER 15TH UPDATE:<br /><br />Alrighty...after much thought - and despite the ending - this book was lovely and well worth a 4.5-star rating.</span>

<div id="review_518118817" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/518118817" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/518118817?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=young-adult-books">young-adult-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=wonderful">wonderful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=supernatural-stuff">supernatural-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=wish-i-could-write-like-this">wish-i-could-write-like-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=pretty-good">pretty-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=thank-god-no-silly-romance">thank-god-no-silly-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer518118817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10280151044060964511">For book 2 Enshadowed, see my review here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/535736292'>http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/...</a><br/><br/>I've decided to take some time to pimp my Nevermore's fanart here:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481815161i/21458265._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“Lady Ligeia," he began again, "is a woman in the literature who returns from the dead, taking over another woman's body to be with her true love."<br/><br/>"Oh, yes. Lovely" Isobel blanched. "I guess the other chick didn't mind at all?” </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/>Being a Poe's devotee ever since I was a secondary school student, I was excited to come across Nevermore which takes u</span>
  <span id="freeText10280151044060964511" style="display:none">For book 2 Enshadowed, see my review here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/535736292">http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/...</a><br><br>I've decided to take some time to pimp my Nevermore's fanart here:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481815161i/21458265._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Lady Ligeia," he began again, "is a woman in the literature who returns from the dead, taking over another woman's body to be with her true love."<br><br>"Oh, yes. Lovely" Isobel blanched. "I guess the other chick didn't mind at all?” </i>
</blockquote><br><br><br>Being a Poe's devotee ever since I was a secondary school student, I was excited to come across Nevermore which takes us to an adventure through the Poeland (hahaha).<br><br>Before reading Nevermore, I have my fair share of Poe-related produces, like Matthew Pearl's <i>The Poe Shadow: A Novel</i>, the eerily attractive <i>Spirits Of the Dead -three tales of the macabre-</i> which was co-worked by three legendary directors (Federico Fellini among them), and Jan Svankmajer's highly imaginative film <i>Lunacy</i>, which is a hallucinating crossover between Poe and, surprise surprise, Marquis de Sade. <br><br>But some of the encounters aren't as pleasing. For example I once watched a gay soft-core porn/horror movie in a Poe's disguise:<i> Edgar Allan Poe's The Raven</i> (I didn't realize it's a gay porn when I bought it), for your own safety please avoid this low-budget film like plague! As a gay porn there's nothing sexy and exciting about the pseudo-porn scenes (they didn't even have the decency to make a worthy smut scene damnit), as a thriller the plot makes absolutely no sense, and I suspect none of the actors knew what they were doing. That's just awful.<br><br>Back to Nevermore itself, I agree that the book is a page-turner, also an enjoyable story to read. Whenever there's a scene of suspense, of dark shadow lurking, or intensive plot-twists, Miss Creagh always delivered. The author cleverly and skillfully weaves many known facts about Poe's life and his mysterious death (e.g. The Poe Toaster) into the plot, then related Poe's works with the mysteries of a haunted 'dreamland' (a parallel world outside of the real world) and the highschool plot which takes place in 'reality'. I'd say the characters setting is also quite unusual. First we get Isobel, a popular cheerleader as the main character. Well, a cheerleader is probably the last person I'd have expected to appear in a Poe-related story, but I appreciate the author's nontraditional choice. Isobel is being set up as a girl who knew next to nothing about Poe and his achievement, so through her point of view, we can get some non-fan's opinions on Poe's works. And I think it's quite an interesting setting.<br><br>We also have Varen as the male lead, Varen is a typical gloomy, unpopular Goth teen, whose name seems to be purposefully familiar with 'Raven'. So who is Varen's favorite author? Edgar Allan Poe. There isn't much of a surprise. For it's pretty difficult for a reader who's drawn to the dark side of life and the beauty of death and decay, not to be fascinated by Poe's writing.<br><br>So when Isobel and Varen were paired (unwillingly) to do a Eng Lit. project together, it also wasn't a surprise for Varen to decide they would base their project on Poe's life and works. <br><br>So far, we got two characters whose characters are pretty much opposite with each another, who came from two entirely different backgrounds, neither of them like each other much at the beginning, and they must cooperate to finish a project together, while Isobel knew next to nothing about Poe (saves the scandalous fact that he married his 13 years old cousin) so she must start from the basic and begin her journey through the gloomy Poeland as a newbie. Okay, so far we have a very interesting setting. Good job, Miss Creagh.<br><br>Even though I'd looked forward to Isobel's exploration through the Poeland, but it turns out the progress of Isobel's learning more about Poe is a rather rushy one, Isobel's own opinion on neither the author nor his works, is largely missing. We only got to see her read through The Masque of the Red Death then commented on it and there's no more mention of her opinion on Poe's works. For starter, I want to know what Isobel would think when she comes across Poe's romance-focused poems and novellas, e.g. Annabelle Lee and Ligeia. Hell, Poe got so many stories which are heavily romance related! So as a young girl who was currently in a relationship (with a popular boy in her group), wouldn't Isobel have came up with some opinions on Poe's expression of romantic, dark love?<br><br>While reading the book, I noticed Nevermore is clearly its author's labor of love, by someone who adores Poe's works of art. Miss Creagh as a newcomer novelist has brilliant ideas, however some of her ideas aren't particularly well excised. For example, Varen and Isobel were forced to spend time together to do their project, but it turns out they spent far little time doing the actual researching and studying for said project, at least it looks this way in Isobel's case, far too little time is spent on the project to my liking. (Varen is being set up as a Poe's fan, so I'll let his lack of time spending on the project pass)<br><br>Still, I must point out I enjoy how Isobel made it through their project's presentation, it's a very interesting part of the story.<br><br>Plus comparing with Isobel, Varen is pretty much a vague character, there are so many things about him we don't know, e.g. his family's background, the reason why he had such a bad relationship with his dad, how he discovered Poe and became the way he was now, etc. After finishing Nevermore I'd very much love to learn more about him, therefore I seriously hope Miss Creagh will write more about Varen in the sequel. Yes, I already learnt enough about Isobel, so next time it should be Varen's turn.^^<br><br>*slight plot spoiler warning*<br><br>Also, it is never explained whether it was Poe's powerful imagination created the dreamland and the demons in it; or did the dreamland had always been in existence before Poe and later Varen stumbled upon it and got trapped? Again, I hope more detail will be revealed in the sequel. <br><br>Much to my surprise, Nevermore offers us no happy ending in the end, and that's why we're left to wait for the sequel. Still.......given the nature of this story's inspiration: Edgar Allan Poe, I can hardly object the lack of a typical happy ending.<br><br>*end of spoiler*<br><br>The Final Words: Miss Creagh's Nevermore is a very ambitious Young Adult novel which manages to bring its mystery and dark fantasy to life, even though being a YA, part of story feels a little bit tamed and a little too 'safe', plus the length of the story can be trimmed a little. Still as a whole, Nevermore is a worthy read for Poe's and/or Goth's fans. I'm looking forward to the sequel. <br><br>PS: If you still want more Poe's inspired stories, I suggest you to try out <i>Poe : 19 new tales of suspense, dark fantasy, and horror inspired by Edgar Allan Poe</i>. Not all of the stories are brilliant, but I strongly recommend outstanding stories like Kim Newman's hilarious "Illimitable Domain".<br><br><i>Edited@09/06/2016: thoughts after re-reading:</i><br><br>To be honest, after this re-reading I found it is getting harder to ignore or tolerate the high school romance parts of the story, I found those high school scenes over-the-top and melodramatic, and it also takes up about 2/3 of the story! As to the male lead Varen, some fans view him as some kind of Gothic-dark-prince-dreamboat but I definitely don't view him as such. Don't get me wrong, I think Varen is okay as a friend and a classmate, but his brooding and emotional nature and his sometime-over-the-top mood swings can be annoying at time (although in this book I can see where he came from, but still). I mean, he should have been an even-better-written character to justify Isobel's obsession with him.<br><br>Before I make it sound like I hate this book...now let's get to the parts that I enjoy! The surreal/nightmarish scenes are superb and spooky, all the Poe-references are finely used and each of them had been planted nicely into the plots, and the ending is suspenseful and super spooky! I still love the scenes with the ghostly villains showing up! (e.g. Pinfeather! He is such a cute, murderous sweetheart!) I will definitely re-read the sequel: <i>Endshadowed</i> ASAP!<br><br><i>Edited@08/05/2017:</i><br><br>It's the third time I read this book! Surely I can see the weakness of the story and characters even more clearly now, still the ending part of the story does save this book!<br><br>Pimping: my drawings for Ligeia: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://vampirekiki.deviantart.com/gallery/38167695/Drawings-of-Ligeia">http://vampirekiki.deviantart.com/gal...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10280151044060964511" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_155015151" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155015151" />
    <a title="Afton Nelson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/857658-afton-nelson"><img alt="Afton Nelson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344825258p2/857658.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155015151?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Afton Nelson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Afton Nelson" href="/user/show/857658-afton-nelson">Afton Nelson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/857658-afton-nelson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/857658-afton-nelson?shelf=bites-mouth-tastes-blood">bites-mouth-tastes-blood</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155015151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15021956355815988705">Problems with this book:<br/><b>Way too long.</b> I can't imagine what this tome must have weighed pre-edit. The descriptions went on and on and on. I got to the point where I'd just read the first sentence or two and start skipping ahead till I got to the action. <br/><br/><b>Plot Insanity</b> The whole plot hinges around the fact that main character Isobel's entire crew (don't get me started on how annoying it is that a HS senior would refer to her group of friends as "her crew.") ostracizes her for something completely o</span>
  <span id="freeText15021956355815988705" style="display:none">Problems with this book:<br /><b>Way too long.</b> I can't imagine what this tome must have weighed pre-edit. The descriptions went on and on and on. I got to the point where I'd just read the first sentence or two and start skipping ahead till I got to the action. <br /><br /><b>Plot Insanity</b> The whole plot hinges around the fact that main character Isobel's entire crew (don't get me started on how annoying it is that a HS senior would refer to her group of friends as "her crew.") ostracizes her for something completely out of her control: her English teacher assigns her a partner for a project who they don't like--creepy, emo, monotone Varen. Even her father, a seemingly really cool guy, is mad she's paired up with him and has problems letting her meet with him to work on their assignment. Really? That just didn't fly with me.<br /><br /><b>Character Inconsistencies</b> The dad seems nice. Cool even. But for some reason Isobel can't confide in him that her boyfriend is a jerk? That doesn't seem right. His freak-out at seeing Varen in his home--not consistent with his character at all. <br /><br /><b>Plot Insanity Take 2</b> The supernatural element is superconfusing. She should have been told what was going on sooner than 500 pages. I should have been told what was going on sooner than 500 pages.<br /><br /><b>Cliche-orama</b> Every high school cliche is crammed into this book. Including the no-brainer "how the lunchroom is divided into cliques" explanation. I believe when our planet is invaded by aliens, even <i>they</i> will not need to have this phenomenon explained. <br /><br /><b>Plot Insanity Take 3</b> The emphasis on "this girl can save herself" was overdone. It was all Isobel. Would it be so bad to have a boy help out? I got the feeling that the author was trying to distance herself from the "Twilight Model" even though the rest of the book follows it quite closely.<br /><br /><b>Ending</b> Ugh! Really? You are forcing me to read Book 2?<br /><br />Good things about this book:<br /><b>Varen</b> Very interesting guy, would have liked to have known more about him. Which, unfortunately, is why I will pick up book 2. This book left him seeming weak and tortured, but I know there is more to him. (See Problems with Ending)<br /><br /><b>Gwen</b> Liked her a lot, even though the quirky friend is a little cliche. (See Problems with Cliche-orama)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15021956355815988705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
