<div id="review_133161573" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/133161573" />
    <a title="Morgan F" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2941288-morgan-f"><img alt="Morgan F" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262298598p2/2941288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/133161573?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morgan F" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morgan F" href="/user/show/2941288-morgan-f">Morgan F</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=pretty-covers">pretty-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=goodreads-author">goodreads-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=awesome-titles">awesome-titles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer133161573" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15691685560420780993">This is one of those books I was reeaaally hoping to love. All my friends did. But, honestly, I don't see how. It wasn't anything special.<br/><br/>For one thing, I found it unrealistic. Yes, I know its a paranormal, but that should make it illogical, not unrealistic. In real life, at least at my school, there is very little open hostility between goths and jocks. Sly commentary, maybe but straight out violence? Nope. And truthfully, there are few goths anymore. Most of them turned either <a href='http://www.urbandictionary.com/define.php?term=emo' rel='nofollow noopener'>emo</a> or <a href='http://www.urbandictionary.com/define.php?term=scene' rel='nofollow noopener'>scene</a>. An</span>
  <span id="freeText15691685560420780993" style="display:none">This is one of those books I was reeaaally hoping to love. All my friends did. But, honestly, I don't see how. It wasn't anything special.<br /><br />For one thing, I found it unrealistic. Yes, I know its a paranormal, but that should make it illogical, not unrealistic. In real life, at least at my school, there is very little open hostility between goths and jocks. Sly commentary, maybe but straight out violence? Nope. And truthfully, there are few goths anymore. Most of them turned either <a href="http://www.urbandictionary.com/define.php?term=emo" rel="nofollow noopener">emo</a> or <a href="http://www.urbandictionary.com/define.php?term=scene" rel="nofollow noopener">scene</a>. And of course the main character <i>had</i> to be a cheerleader (the stereotyped opposite of gothness) and her boyfriend <i>had</i> to be a quarterback because thats just how the world works, dunnit? It just didn't seem true for me. I don't know. Maybe things are different in the South. <br /><br />I didn't like the writing. I prefer first person. I dislike third person that wants to be first person. There were sentences like: "Isobel tried the door. There was no one there. Duh". Who is the one duhing? Isobel or the narrator who thinks like Isobel? And I didn't like the random quips. I found them a little cheesy and unfunny. <br /><br />I wasn't a big fan of either Isobel and Varen. They were stereotypical, and Isobel annoyed the heck out of me. I kept wanting to call her Brittney for some reason. She was very rash, sort of immature, and quite cheesy. She didn't <i>quite</i> make it on my annoying characters shelf, but she was close. Varen, I'm sorry ladies, but he was boring. He did nothing. If he was a girl, everyone would call him out for being bithcy, but since he is a guy that is somehow sexy. And besides, there is only one goth boy in my life: Erik Derenksi. Hear that Erik?! We are gonna get maaaaaarried!! Aw, don't run away! *shrugs* He acts like he hates me, but he loves me. He does. And guess what, Kim! He hates babies too! You guys can sit on them together. Oh whats that in the distance? Hmm, I believe it is my point, running far far away from here........Anyway, Varen did not make me swoon.<br /><br />Oh, and Gwen? A totally obvious plot device. She appears out of nowhere at the most convenient times. I wish I had a friend that was willing to drop everything to deal with the drama in my life. <br /><br />And I felt the end was inconsistent with the rest of the novel. The beginning was slow-going, a crazed raven here, a funky dream there, but the end was like WHOOSH. Kind of like the Incredible Hulk coaster at Universal Studios. Here you are just cruising along the track, chugga chugga chugga, then KABMLAM! You are being shot of cannon and taking an upside-down plunge. The ending was just some crazy paranormal hodgepodge. I nearly got whiplash. The pacing and content didn't match, and that bothered me. <br /><br />Overall, meh. Nitpicks aside, I liked it but I never got the OMG THIS IS SO GOOD feeling. It was a solid three stars, but I'll give it a virtual half-star more because I think the cover, particularly Isobel, is gorgeous. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15691685560420780993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_598645734" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/598645734" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14811808-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585394064p2/14811808.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/598645734?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/14811808-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=favourite-hero">favourite-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=worth-re-reading">worth-re-reading</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer598645734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3891384417298947734"><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380418862i/829749.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/><blockquote>
  <b>“There is no exquisite beauty… without some strangeness in the proportion.”</b>
</blockquote><br/>When Isobel is paired with Varen for the English class project, she is horrified. Varen is dark and cold and sarcastic and there are lots of rumors about him that make being around him quite uncomfortable. <br/>Firstly, she only wants to recieve a good mark, but soon it is not about the project anymore. There is something about Varen and his piercing eyes and Isobel does not know what it is, but she cannot resist being</span>
  <span id="freeText3891384417298947734" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380418862i/829749.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><blockquote>
  <b>“There is no exquisite beauty… without some strangeness in the proportion.”</b>
</blockquote><br>When Isobel is paired with Varen for the English class project, she is horrified. Varen is dark and cold and sarcastic and there are lots of rumors about him that make being around him quite uncomfortable. <br>Firstly, she only wants to recieve a good mark, but soon it is not about the project anymore. There is something about Varen and his piercing eyes and Isobel does not know what it is, but she cannot resist being with this gloomy Goth. <br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380418862i/829750.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><blockquote>
  <b>“When there is no way, you must make a way.”</b>
</blockquote> <br>I was immediately in love with Varen and his piercing eyes and I loved him even more after he said that Sir Edgar Allan Poe is a <i>literary god</i>. <br>I love this poet and all his works and I loved all the poems that were mentioned. I loved the way Varen felt about these poems and how he treasured them. <br><blockquote>
  <b>Just because I wear black and keep a private journal, that doesn't mean I'm going to blow up the school. Or terrorize mindless cheerleaders, for that matter.”</b>
</blockquote><br>Varen was a very deep character with his own skeletons in the closet and dark secrets. He was far more than he pretended to be and he controlled his actions and words perfectly. Furthermore, I loved his gaze and his inner strength and determination. <br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380418862i/829751.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>Isobel was nothing like she seemed. I generally have a problem with the sunny, perfect-girl characters, but Isobel was definitely different. <br>Firstly, she was rather open-minded and though she had a problem with Varen being a Goth at the beginning, it soon changed. She was ready to listen and to learn. To ask for forgiveness and to forgive. Besides, she always said what was on her mind, even if it was embarassing and uncomfortable. She was a very strong and refreshing protagonist, intelligent and authentic.<br><blockquote>
  <b>“Hands quivering, she reached toward him.<br>"Don't." He turned his back to her, facing the door.<br>That word had stopped her once before. But not now. Not now that she had glimpsed through the funeral front of Varen's own eternal Grim Facade. Despite all the dark armor, the kohl eye liner, the black boots and chains, she saw him clearly now. She peered through the curtain of that cruel calmness, through the death stare and the vampire sentiments and angst and, behind it all, had found true beauty.”</b>
</blockquote><br>I loved Gwen, she was absolutely a kick-ass friend and I loved Isobel's family. The write style of the author was fluent and intriguing, it was absolutely impossible to put this book down after picking it up. <br>And another aspect I loved about this book was the relationship between Isobel and Varen. It built up rather slow and became stronger and stronger until there was a deep and bittersweet connection between these characters. <br><br>The final part broke my heart. Finally, all the questions were answered and the situation escalated, it was thrilling and creepy and heart-breaking at the same time. I loved it, but I thought I would die when I read the last page... <br>I loved this book from the first until the last page and I loved both Varen and Isobel.<br><blockquote>
  <b>“My beautiful, my Isobel. My Love. You ask me to wait. And so I wait.<br>For all of this, I know, is but a dream.<br>And when, in sleep, at last we wake,<br>I will see you again.”</b>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="3891384417298947734" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_400838601" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/400838601" />
    <a title="Anzu The Great Destroyer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer"><img alt="Anzu The Great Destroyer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455829739p2/2278800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/400838601?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anzu The Great Destroyer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anzu The Great Destroyer" href="/user/show/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer">Anzu The Great Destroyer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781442402034" href="/book/show/9337673-nevermore">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=must-reads">must-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=great-concept">great-concept</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=watch-your-step-cliffs-ahead">watch-your-step-cliffs-ahead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=zomg-i-must-have-him">zomg-i-must-have-him</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=ya-is-dead">ya-is-dead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=paranormal-fix">paranormal-fix</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=evil-satan">evil-satan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=reviewed-2012">reviewed-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer400838601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4060951382203595988">I was not going to write a review for <i>Nevermore</i> because it was one of those books that kept me reading mouth open, eyes wide, fingers stuck not able to type in any ideas. Then again, I felt like writing a review would push you guys into giving this book a try. Which you should totally do, by the way. It’s awesome.<br/><br/>Since I’m short on ideas and irritated because of a stupid allergy, I’m afraid my review won’t be much fun. Nor interesting. Not aggravating. Nor.. something else that I can’t think of.</span>
  <span id="freeText4060951382203595988" style="display:none">I was not going to write a review for <i>Nevermore</i> because it was one of those books that kept me reading mouth open, eyes wide, fingers stuck not able to type in any ideas. Then again, I felt like writing a review would push you guys into giving this book a try. Which you should totally do, by the way. It’s awesome.<br><br>Since I’m short on ideas and irritated because of a stupid allergy, I’m afraid my review won’t be much fun. Nor interesting. Not aggravating. Nor.. something else that I can’t think of. Oh yes, I remembered. Nor making much sense.<br><br>No, no it will make sense. It will make sense only if you read <i>Nevermore</i>.<br><br>Which you should.<br><br>Okay then, I’ll go on telling you why I loved it so much. See, I’m not the biggest fan of cheerleaders. The MC is a cheerleader. Dating the highschool’s football star. Not a good student. The usual. I didn’t think I would like Isobel. Hell, I hated her at the beginning of the book. But Kelly Creagh, being an amazing author as she is, made Isobel evolve into an admirable character.<br><br>The story revolving Poe was interesting enough. We get even some nice quotes from his works. Even though the story mostly goes around the school assignment, it did not get boring. The other part went around the dreamworld, which could get confusing. The trick is to pay total attention to the book in these moments. This means that you should read it in complete silence, when no one can interrupt. Worked for me like a charm.<br><br>And last but not least, the reason why I loved <i>Nevermore</i> so much is Varen. This goth baby won me over fair and square.<br><br>I love, absolutely love, hot goth guys. He’s also deep, he’s an artist. He writes and draws. Sigh. This is the perfect Varen:<br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380389089i/750080._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Isn’t he nice? @_@<br><br>So there you have it. Is title the book for you? Take this quick quiz and find out!<br><br>1. Do you like reading books?<br>a. yes (1 point)<br>b. no (0 points)<br><br>2. Do you like hot goth guys?<br>a. yes (1 point)<br>b. no (0 points)<br><br>If your answer score is 2 or higher, then <i>Nevermore</i> is the book for you.<br><br>Read it.<br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380389089i/750081._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Review also posted on<br><a href="http://zombiehazard.blogspot.com/2012/12/nevermore-nevermore-1.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340428i/696822.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Read #1: 15th - 18th Nov 2012<br>Read #2: 28th - 29th Jul 2015</span>

<div id="review_1399429178" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1399429178" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17688793-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601659534p2/17688793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1399429178?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/17688793-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781442402010" href="/book/show/10367314-nevermore">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17688793-laura?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17688793-laura?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17688793-laura?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17688793-laura?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1399429178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13054304175642822317"><b>Is <i>all</i> that we see or seem<br/>But a dream within a dream?</b><br/><br/>This was my second time reading <i>Nevermore</i> and it's safe to say that I loved it just as much as the first time around. I stayed up until three last night to finish it because I just couldn't get enough of the sinister world Kelly Creagh created. Also, I couldn't for the life of me remember some very important details which is why, at times, it felt like I was reading it for the first time. Thanks, brain, for forgetting almost everything that ha</span>
  <span id="freeText13054304175642822317" style="display:none"><b>Is <i>all</i> that we see or seem<br>But a dream within a dream?</b><br><br>This was my second time reading <i>Nevermore</i> and it's safe to say that I loved it just as much as the first time around. I stayed up until three last night to finish it because I just couldn't get enough of the sinister world Kelly Creagh created. Also, I couldn't for the life of me remember some very important details which is why, at times, it felt like I was reading it for the first time. Thanks, brain, for forgetting almost everything that happens during the last 150-200 pages! <br><br>Now, for this review I thought I'd just make a recipe sort of thing and present you the ingredients that made <i>Nevermore</i> such a spectacular read. <br><br><b>Ingredient #1:</b> Edgar Allan Poe<br><br>Because whose tales and poems would make a better foundation for a gothic and slightly creepy book about disappearing into otherworldly dreams? I can't think of anyone suited better than Mr. Poe. His stories and verses were so seamlessly woven into and intertwined with this story and added just the right amount of literature and grotesquerie.<br>I never even read any of Poe's tales or poems before I was introduced to his genius through this book and actually bought a special edition of his complete collection, just like the one Varen has in <i>Nevermore</i>. So not only did his stories enhance this one in the most beautiful way, but it also introduced me to a writer whose works I might never have bothered with otherwise. <br><br><b>Ingredient #2:</b> Likable Heroine<br><br>“Just because I live in the sunlight, enjoy being blond, and wear a cheerleading uniform, that doesn't mean I'm stupid. I'm so sick of that.”<br><br>Yes, Isobel Lanley is a cheerleader, and a pretty good one at that. And yes, she's also dating Mr. Popular, football player Brad in the beginning of the book. So yes, I must admit <i>Nevermore</i> starts out a little cliché, and while that never bothered me, it might some people. But really, don't let that deter you. Give the book a chance and wait it out because later there'll be no trace of it. And Isobel, while being a cheerleader and all that, is actually a great heroine, albeit at times a bit clueless. She doesn't let others pressure her into unhealthy relationships and actually recognizes them as such. She stands up to bullies and isn't afraid to do her own thing. I really enjoyed that. All in all she came across as a pretty realistic 16 year old.<br><br><b>Ingredient #3:</b> Interesting Hero<br><br>“Just because I wear black and keep a private journal, that doesn't mean I'm going to blow up the school. Or terrorize mindless cheerleaders, for that matter.”<br><br>Yep, Varen Nethers definitely belongs to the gothic crowd of Trenton High and with his lip ring and dyed hair he couldn't be farther from Isobel's world of pom poms and meatheads *cough* Brad *cough*. I was intrigued with Varen from the moment he first showed up in the story. Everything about him kind of fascinated me. His beautiful handwriting, always in purple. The little black notebook he always carries around. His obsession with everything Edgar Allan Poe. His cool and scowling demeanor. Because who doesn't like some teenage angst? I wanted to know more about him, find out how he became the way he is. You could say I was a little obsessed myself. And firmly stayed that way throughout the book. I loved seeing him warm up to Isobel! When he started to become a bit playful or when he actually smiled I nearly died. I love all sides of his character and can't wait to read more about him in the sequel, <i>Enshadowed</i>. <br><br><b>Ingredient #4:</b> THE CHEMISTRY ♥<br><br>Varen and Isobel, how much I love them. In spite of some other clichés, their story is in no way one of insta love and for that I am forever grateful. When the two of them first have to interact with each other - yes, I admit, they're partnered for an English project against their will, but WHO CARES. Those things happen all the time in school - well, they don't like each other. As I already mentioned above, they're from different high school worlds. He thinks she's some dumb, blond bimbo, and she thinks he's <s>slightly</s> okay very creepy. But because of that their chemistry has time to evolve slowly and perfectly. As the reader, you barely notice how their feelings change because of the subtle way it's done, and next thing you know you're shipping them so hard and you don't even know how it happened. The pace is restrained and beautiful and just the way I like it. <br><br><b>Ingredient #5:</b> The Sidekicks<br><br>Because let's be real, they are so important to every story! Gwen, the girl who saves Isobel from a depressing friendless existence after the fall-out with her former clique, is my absolute favorite and gives the otherwise dark read some truly needed funny scenes. She's straight-forward, honest and has an outgoing, slightly crazed demeanor. She provided some laugh-out-loud moments and is the best friend every YA heroine needs. <br>There's also this other guy who will remain nameless in this review because you need to meet him yourself. He's in the habit of talking like a fortune cookie and only showing up when it pleases him, which just made him even more mysterious and interesting. I can't wait to find out what odd things he'll say or do in the next book. <br><br><b>Ingredient #6:</b> The Atmosphere<br><br>Kelly Creagh really knows how to take some Victorian horror lit and a few good old high school kids and turn that into an absolute page-turner. I loved the creatures she added to Poe's gory stories and how she created a nightmarish dreamworld out of it. Reading Poe's tales and poems, and then finding bits and pieces in this book was so much fun. And even if you don't read them, Poe's verses are included where they're needed.<br>Creagh's writing is extremely beautiful, especially when it comes to describing the scenes in the dreamworld later on. The way she makes Poe's stories come to life is magical and enthralling.<br><br><b>Deep into that darkness peering,<br>long I stood there wondering, fearing,<br>Doubting, dreaming dreams no mortal<br>ever dared to dream before.</b><br><br>- Edgar Allan Poe, "The Raven"<br><br>I definitely recommend you give this book a try. Especially next month around Halloween would be the perfect time to dive into the world of Varen and Isobel. <br>For me all that's left now is impatiently waiting for tomorrow, when the sequel will finally be in my hands. (It better be, Amazon, or else!)<br><br><i>Find me on the blog:</i><br><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/lauras-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>

<div id="review_105987383" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105987383" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105987383?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Arlene by: </span>
      TBR Reduction Challenge #2 - Flannery 
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=ya-paranormal">ya-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105987383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5465451671942065930"><b>Rating Clarification: 4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><b>Absolutely I.N.C.R.E.D.I.B.L.E!!!</b><br/><br/>I have so many great things to say about <b>Nevermore</b>, but I’d rather you read the book than hear me ramble about what a great YA paranormal read this is, so I’m just going to choose a few things that really stood out for me. By no means does this cover all of the great things I have to say about this book that I finished in two short days because it was absolutely unputdownable!!<br/><br/>First, the paranormal aspect of this novel was perfectly</span>
  <span id="freeText5465451671942065930" style="display:none"><b>Rating Clarification: 4.5 Stars</b><br /><br /><b>Absolutely I.N.C.R.E.D.I.B.L.E!!!</b><br /><br />I have so many great things to say about <b>Nevermore</b>, but I’d rather you read the book than hear me ramble about what a great YA paranormal read this is, so I’m just going to choose a few things that really stood out for me. By no means does this cover all of the great things I have to say about this book that I finished in two short days because it was absolutely unputdownable!!<br /><br />First, the paranormal aspect of this novel was perfectly executed. However, when I say paranormal, I have to warn you; you won’t find any vampires, werewolves, faries or witches in this book, but that doesn’t stop it from being one of the better books out there IMHO. What I loved was that the author didn’t rush into the paranormal aspect of this story, so as the storyline was transitioning, my mind was ready for a reality suspension, and it just happened naturally. And, holy PINFEATHERS what a ride!!<br /><br />Next, I’ve read a few of Edgar Allen Poe’s works when I was in high school, and I’ve always liked his gothic, creepy style. So to see Creagh use Poe’s tales and mysterious death as the engine to kick start this ride was refreshing, creative and perfectly done. After reading this book, I’m motivated to dive into his writing again because the author did an absolutely POE-fect job blending his style with her imaginative story to take the reader on a mystical, gothic adventure. Loved it!<br /><br />Lastly, what a refreshing take to offer up a story where the MC has a healthy, positive relationship with her family. Nice to know they actually exist out there. I loved it! I liked Isobel’s relationship with her mom, dad and younger brother. I also loved how the relationship between her and Varen wasn’t shoved down the reader’s throat in the first few chapters. The author developed that part slowly and ultimately made it feel real and genuine.<br /><br />Yet another book that’s been sitting on my shelf when I should have picked it up a long time ago. I’m so glad I was challenged to read <b>Nevermore</b> because I had no idea how much I was going to LOVE this book!!<br /><br />The only reason I’m removing ½ a star is because the ending has a hellava painful cliffy and second Varen kept going missing every time I wanted more of him. Other than that A.W.E.S.O.M.E! L.O.V.E.D I.T!!! Read it N.O.W! <br /><br /><br />.<br />.<br />.<br /><br />Once again, thank you Flannery for challenging me to read this book. You are the bestest challenge book chooser! :D</span>

<div id="review_174282831" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/174282831" />
    <a title="Samantha Young" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4394330-samantha-young"><img alt="Samantha Young" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593532204p2/4394330.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/174282831?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha Young" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha Young" href="/user/show/4394330-samantha-young">Samantha Young</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4394330-samantha-young?shelf=favourite-authors">favourite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4394330-samantha-young?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4394330-samantha-young?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4394330-samantha-young?shelf=ya-paranormal">ya-paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174282831" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1108971769224629152">Well they say never judge a book by its cover. ‘Tis true. ‘Tis true. I would not have picked up Nevermore if it hadn’t been for an extremely well-written review that absolutely raved about it.<br/>I am so glad I picked it up.<br/>Kelly Creagh has created one of the most vivid worlds I have ever discovered. If a book could be described as IMAX then Nevermore is that book; the characters and scenes sprang from the pages of the book to play out in front of me in striking clarity. In a word, it was wonderful.</span>
  <span id="freeText1108971769224629152" style="display:none">Well they say never judge a book by its cover. ‘Tis true. ‘Tis true. I would not have picked up Nevermore if it hadn’t been for an extremely well-written review that absolutely raved about it.<br />I am so glad I picked it up.<br />Kelly Creagh has created one of the most vivid worlds I have ever discovered. If a book could be described as IMAX then Nevermore is that book; the characters and scenes sprang from the pages of the book to play out in front of me in striking clarity. In a word, it was wonderful. I don’t know what I was expecting. Perhaps a run-of-the-mill supernatural teen romance. But Nevermore is so much MORE. It’s gothic and creepy as all hell sometimes, but there is also a perfect blend of realism and social drama. I loved how Creagh highlighted the cliques at high school and the way certain people are seen for the way they look and act – goths, jocks, cheerleaders etc. She does this without being cliché, and actually brings attention to the often dangerous consequences of making people feel ‘other’. <br />As for the characters of Nevermore… I fell in love with them all. Isobel is the perfect teen girl’s voice. She cares about school and cheerleading and what her friends think about her, but the slight shallowness of what she deems important is offset by the strength of her character. And Isobel is definitely a strong character with an ingrained sense of right and wrong. Best of all she has the courage to go against the grain and stand up for what’s right when she sees wrongdoing. <br />Varen is that guy in school I would have had a crush on; dark and broody with the soul of a poet. He can be sarcastic and cold but he has a vulnerable side and a great backstory, and who doesn’t love that in a hero?<br />Other characters that really shone for me were Danny – Isobel’s annoying and hilarious little brother (the sibling relationship was beautifully described, I really believed in it) – and Gwen, who is quite possibly one of the funniest, quirkiest and likeable sidekicks in YA fiction.<br />The supernatural element of Nevermore is really different; Creagh’s use of Edgar Allen Poe’s works to build a storyworld is so original and fantastically done, and having not read everything by Poe there was probably some great subtleties I didn’t even pick up on. As I said, this is gothic YA, and there are some very creepy moments, all of which kept me hooked and intrigued. <br />I can’t believe I have to wait until 2012 for the next book. Not fair.<br /><br />Darkly beautiful and utterly captivating. <br /><br />Five Massive Massive Stars!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1108971769224629152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_124968912" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124968912" />
    <a title="Annabelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1235083-annabelle"><img alt="Annabelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348368292p2/1235083.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<div id="review_96285171" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96285171" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3471319-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512402337p2/3471319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96285171?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/3471319-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3471319-jen?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3471319-jen?shelf=paid-full-price">paid-full-price</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3471319-jen?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96285171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer860121930406237143">Disclaimer: This review will contain badly-structured paragraphs and thoughts that are erratic and have nothing to do with one another, other than the absolute incoherant fangirlness I'm experiencing at this time. <br/><br/><br/>From the first time I laid my eyes on this book sometime in 2009, when Amazon recommended I check it out, I knew this would be a special relationship. The blacks and the purples and the guy on the cover with his brooding stare. I didn't even know what this book was about and I needed i</span>
  <span id="freeText860121930406237143" style="display:none">Disclaimer: This review will contain badly-structured paragraphs and thoughts that are erratic and have nothing to do with one another, other than the absolute incoherant fangirlness I'm experiencing at this time. <br /><br /><br />From the first time I laid my eyes on this book sometime in 2009, when Amazon recommended I check it out, I knew this would be a special relationship. The blacks and the purples and the guy on the cover with his brooding stare. I didn't even know what this book was about and I needed it. Then I found out the story was heavily influenced by Poe. *dies* I've been intrigued by Poe since I was 10. My parents bought me the complete works for Christmas, at my request, and I loved it. I couldn't understand most of it, but that's okay. I knew what I liked. And the macabre was definitely something I liked. <br /><br />So in this story, we have Poe lore. We have a story involving the mystery that is Poe. We have a story incorporating the mysteries written by Poe. We have the macabre. We have some SERIOUS tension, anticipation, and one of the most heartfelt romances between yummy, brooding Varen and sharp-witted Isobel. We have a sexalicious cover. All of this equals a 540ish page piece of YA awesomeness. <br /><br />This story was not long enough. I did not feel at all that it was 540 pages. Never once did I get bored. The way that the romance between polar opposites Varen Nethers and Isobel Lanley was slowly and realistically crafted seriously almost made my heart burst with butterflies. I hate to say it, but I've not felt this much anticipation and sexual tension between two characters since Twilight. Do not let that steer you away, anti-Twilight people. I can't even count how many times I was internally doing backflips because I thought, "this is it. They're going to kiss and make out and be in love forever and ever because Varen is perfect and I heart him." Only to have that hope snatched away by some unforeseen circumstance or another. If this book wasn't so pretty and I didn't love everything about it so much, I would've crossed out some words and improvised a little making out every single paragraph. But I'm not an author, and with good reason.<br /><br />Anyway, Varen. Oh, Varen. What can I say about you that would possibly describe you the way you deserve? Who would've thought a Goth boy could be so enticing? I will say that he is in my top 3 true book loves, though. That's kind of serious. I think the best way to describe the way I feel about him is this: <b>I can has?</b><br /><br />Isobel was a peppy little spitfire. She was snarky and had quite a temper, which I love. She's not afraid to go against the grain of her stupid popular friends. Speaking of stupid popular friends, I hated Brad. HATED HIM. He's the epitome of douche bag. Read this book and I guarantee you will agree with me. Then there are the Nocs, who will probably haunt my nightmares for coming weeks. Pinfeathers was especially creepy. And yet I still felt a pinch of enjoyment whenever I read his name. Very intriguing characters! And to put Reynolds in the story, after knowing the story about Poe calling for "Reynolds" on his death bed, just adds a whole different level of excitement for me.<br />And Gwen. I want a Gwen for myself. She's like the never-shut-up, tactless, overly inquisitive, "OMG take your Adderall" version of Alice Cullen. She has some of the best lines in the book, which I will go back and re-read plenty of times when I need a laugh.<br /><br />Kelly Creagh has done a wonderful thing with this novel. By far one of my top 5 for 2010. I want to read it all over again to make sure I didn't miss anything, which I'm sure I did. I love this novel. I might want to marry it.<br /><br />Please, for the sake of humanity. Go buy this book. I don't care how and I don't care where. Just do it. You won't be disappointed. Except for the fact that there's an extremely painful cliffhanger and there's been no confirmation of the release date for following books. Another source of potential nightmares for months to come :( PLEASE, KELLY CREAGH. I know it's only a day after the release, but I'm dying here and I need more Varen!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="860121930406237143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_388170876" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/388170876" />
    <a title="Holly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2127955-holly"><img alt="Holly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520179670p2/2127955.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/388170876?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Holly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Holly" href="/user/show/2127955-holly">Holly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Poe and character driven YA novels.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=beloved-characters">beloved-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=favorite-heroes">favorite-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=favorite-heroines">favorite-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=obsessively-readable">obsessively-readable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=my-dream-men">my-dream-men</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=best-books-read-in-2012">best-books-read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=dark-and-twisted">dark-and-twisted</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer388170876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8987046996515469454">5++++ stars<br/><br/>It has been so long since I was this excited about a book. Since I was so caught up in a story that all I wanted to do was read. All I wanted to do was be in that world, as creepy and unsettling as it may have been. I wanted to be there....and Creagh totally made me feel like I was right in the middle of all the nightmarish beauty that was Nevermore.<br/><br/>There have been countless reviews detailing the plot (which is beyond brilliant and original, especially in the YA genre), so i will sett</span>
  <span id="freeText8987046996515469454" style="display:none">5++++ stars<br /><br />It has been so long since I was this excited about a book. Since I was so caught up in a story that all I wanted to do was read. All I wanted to do was be in that world, as creepy and unsettling as it may have been. I wanted to be there....and Creagh totally made me feel like I was right in the middle of all the nightmarish beauty that was Nevermore.<br /><br />There have been countless reviews detailing the plot (which is beyond brilliant and original, especially in the YA genre), so i will settle on just giving you a quick rundown of what I thought of the book as a whole.<br /><br />The world building was perfectly done, and Creagh's gorgeous, almost lyrical writing style is perfectly suited to this gothicly nightmarish fairy tale.<br /><br />As for the characters. Holy hell. Where do I even start? I went into this almost expecting Isobel to be this perfectly blonde Barbie doll, and was just hoping I would be able to read the book without her annoying me too much. Imagine my surprise when I realized within the first few pages, that Isobel was so much more than just a pretty face. She was a strong, kick ass character that I ended up loving deeply. And Varen...well, I am not exactly sure what it is about him that made me fall under his spell, but he also ended up capturing my heart. <br /><br />One of the BEST aspects of Nevermore, were the shadowy Dreamworld characters. I will freely admit to my unexplanable love for Pinfeathers. He has to be one of the most memorable and strangely endearing (???!!!) villains I have ever come across. I don't understand why I ended up loving his creepy character so much...but there it is. Also, I will own up to a slight fangirly crush on Reynolds. He's a badass who has a lot to answer for...but a badass nonetheless.<br /><br />Bottom line, this was one of the most incredibly imaginative, and obsessively readable books I have found in ages. Definitely one of the best books I have read all year, and in fact one of my all time favorites as well.<br /><br />It is fitting that Nevermore, much like the characters of Isobel and Varen, ended up being so much more than I expected. I can't wait for the sequel.<br /><br /><br />My YT Channel: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/user/Bookgasmic">http://www.youtube.com/user/Bookgasmic</a><br />My blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://ravingbookaddict.blogspot.com/">http://ravingbookaddict.blogspot.com/</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8987046996515469454" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_84116649" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/84116649" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/84116649?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer84116649" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8101085859322258869">Confession time...*pause for effect* I have never heard of nor read anything by the obviously legendary Edgar Allan Poe before, till I read this book. <br/>*inserts gasps here*<br/>However, this book had me fascinated by his work and will quickly proceed to the nearest book store/library to remedy that fact.<br/><br/>Moving on...<br/><br/>How the hell do I even start this review? Seriously I'm at a lost of words to describe the greatness that is <b>Nevemore</b>.<br/>OMG, WOW, HOLY SHIIIIT? Nope, it doesn't do it justice, in fact, nothin</span>
  <span id="freeText8101085859322258869" style="display:none">Confession time...*pause for effect* I have never heard of nor read anything by the obviously legendary Edgar Allan Poe before, till I read this book. <br />*inserts gasps here*<br />However, this book had me fascinated by his work and will quickly proceed to the nearest book store/library to remedy that fact.<br /><br />Moving on...<br /><br />How the hell do I even start this review? Seriously I'm at a lost of words to describe the greatness that is <b>Nevemore</b>.<br />OMG, WOW, HOLY SHIIIIT? Nope, it doesn't do it justice, in fact, nothing I say will give this book the justice it deserves, so I'll just be rambling on from here on in.<br /><br />I loved every.single.word etched on these pages, Kelly Creagh has captured a dream like escape and made it feel so vividly real that it shocked the hell out me once I closed this book. I mean, <i>dammme</i> is this some seriously sensational story telling!!<br /><br />I'm just going to start with Varen Nethers, cause lets face it, he's the soul of this entire epic story.<br />Varen is probably with out a doubt the most complex and intense character I have ever read, that's right Edward Cullen, push over, your not complex enough me no longer.<br />Everything about him is enticing and intriguing, his look, his mannerisms and his voice. It's not necessarily the words he says (or lack there of) but how he holds every scene with the <i>way</i> he delivers ever calculating vague riddle-like line that makes it some how go right through you. He gives a whole new delicious meaning to the word mysterious. So freaken hauntingly beautiful.<br />If Varen is the soul of this book, then Isobel Lanley is definitely the heart. Her faith and everlasting strength to be a good person, stand up to what she believes in while going through a wide range of unimaginative things <i>and</i> attempts to save the man that she loves from his own escape, merit an 'your totally awesome' in my book. I only cringed once during that whole apology cheer, but then again I've never been for the whole pom-pom-go-team-go thing. Altogether she made an excellent well defined character.<br /><br />The relationship between Varen and Isobel is a strange one. Not your typical hook-up. It never really escalated more then a few conversations and meetings. But, you could feel the pull, the obvious attraction and heated chemistry, but there was always something looming above them, bigger then both and totally in the way. No dramatic declarations, just the underlining understanding of affection that seeps out from every moment that they shared. This annoyed and thrilled me at the same time. I'm a selfish reader and I wanted so much more. Although, there were a lot of moments that just dripped sexy. Who knew getting handed a tub of ice cream could melt me and when he read to her? So romantic. And dear God that heart-stopping, heart-pounding kiss? The ribbon? There are no words. And yet I still wanted more. I understand why it was written this way and in it's own right it's perfect, but yeah, I'm still gonna pout.<br /><br />Hated Isobel's (so called) friends, they all sucked (save for Nikki, Stevie &amp; Gwen) and were annoyingly immature and nasty. That's pretty much all I got for them.<br />I liked Isobel's parents but Varen's dad is an ass and I can totally see why he became Oh-Dark-One cause of him. I'd would have needed the escape too.<br />Pinfeather was amusing in one of those awesome sadistic ways, I know I'm suppose to hate him and all, but he made me laugh.<br />Reynolds adds nicely to this warped story, I hope we see him again in the next book.<br />The plot of the story is mind baffling crazy, taking Varen's self-made escape and balancing it on the tips of reality. It kept me spinning right till the very end of this massive 543 pg book. It never slows down, continuously entertaining making it captivating and unsettling at the same time. <br />Totally creepiness laces through out the story, very shutter worthy giving me the proper heebeejeebees chills and nightmares, but, dammmme, do I want more of where that came from! Can't.wait.for the.sequel.need.it.NOW.<br /><br />I can go on and on and on about the awesomeness that is <s>Varen</s> <b>Nevermore</b>, but y'all get the point. Remarkable-Remarkable writing, well crafted imaginative plot and characters who will have you on your hands and knees begging for(never)more!!<br /><br />Read this book it's an amazing rush!!!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8101085859322258869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer95163736" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12501195239688665582"><i> At last he stopped, and she stared down at the printed column of words, unable to comprehend a single one. His hand, warm and steady, wound its way around hers, wrapping it like a spider would its prey. She surrendered it to him, unable to watch even as his thumb traced the place, just above her knuckles, where he had once written his number in deep violet. Isobel ceased to breathe. Her heart pounded in her chest, her thoughts shattering into senseless fragments. All the while, her eyes remaine</i></span>
  <span id="freeText12501195239688665582" style="display:none"><i> At last he stopped, and she stared down at the printed column of words, unable to comprehend a single one. His hand, warm and steady, wound its way around hers, wrapping it like a spider would its prey. She surrendered it to him, unable to watch even as his thumb traced the place, just above her knuckles, where he had once written his number in deep violet. Isobel ceased to breathe. Her heart pounded in her chest, her thoughts shattering into senseless fragments. All the while, her eyes remained trained and unblinking on the open page. Lines without meaning stared up at her, little more than black sticks in an otherwise white world. </i> <br /><br />I hope that quote incite you to read this book. Because really you should. Nevermore is a breathtaking read from start to finish. <br /><br />The plot it refreshingly different from other YA paranormal reads. I don’t want to say to much, but I will say - no vampires, no werewolves, no angels and mostly importantly no love triangle. It is mysterious, dark and will have you guessing right until the end. The romance in this book is beautifully done, never rushed.<br /><br />They are so many wonderful characters in this story Isobel, Gwen, Reynolds, Danny and of course VAREN. One word for him WOW. I also agree with other reviews that Pinfeathers is entertaining and kind of likeable for a bad guy. They was only one thing that kind of annoyed me. Isobel’s ex friends and ex boyfriend. They really couldn’t have not been stupider. I just wanted to knock their heads together and hopefully some sense into them. <br /><br />The ending major CLIFFHANGER that will leave you begging for more! But don’t let that put you off reading this book because this is one of the few books you shouldn‘t miss. I suggest you run out and get it right now!</span>

<div id="review_2032873207" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2032873207" />
    <a title="Fiona✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64045945-fiona"><img alt="Fiona✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602153070p2/64045945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2032873207?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fiona✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fiona✨" href="/user/show/64045945-fiona">Fiona✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64045945-fiona?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64045945-fiona?shelf=fave-villains">fave-villains</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64045945-fiona?shelf=4-5-star">4-5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64045945-fiona?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64045945-fiona?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64045945-fiona?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64045945-fiona?shelf=beautifully-eerie">beautifully-eerie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64045945-fiona?shelf=best-of-2017">best-of-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64045945-fiona?shelf=i-love-you-anyway">i-love-you-anyway</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64045945-fiona?shelf=i-will-go-down-with-this-ship">i-will-go-down-with-this-ship</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2032873207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9097805325187370305">SOUNDTRACK:<br/><br/>Creeper - Misery<br/>My Chemical Romance - Interlude<br/>From First To Last - Emily<br/>AFI - Silver and Cold<br/><br/>I made a full playlist on my spotify @fionamatilda !! (sometimes the links work and sometimes they don't lol)<br/><br/>----------------------------------<br/><br/>actual rating: 4,5 stars<br/><br/>This is me trying to bring my review schedule back on track once again, wish me luck lol<br/><br/>🌹 A (more or less) quick recap on the turbulent lovestory between me and this book 🌹<br/><br/>I read Nevermore for the first time when I was 17 and I </span>
  <span id="freeText9097805325187370305" style="display:none">SOUNDTRACK:<br /><br />Creeper - Misery<br />My Chemical Romance - Interlude<br />From First To Last - Emily<br />AFI - Silver and Cold<br /><br />I made a full playlist on my spotify @fionamatilda !! (sometimes the links work and sometimes they don't lol)<br /><br />----------------------------------<br /><br />actual rating: 4,5 stars<br /><br />This is me trying to bring my review schedule back on track once again, wish me luck lol<br /><br />🌹 A (more or less) quick recap on the turbulent lovestory between me and this book 🌹<br /><br />I read Nevermore for the first time when I was 17 and I fell in love with everything about it, from the subtle and not-so-subtle nods to Poe, to the characters, to the deliciously dramatic romance, to the fact that this was just so much more unique than all the other paranormal romances I've read before.<br />In fact, I was so obsessed with it that I immediately ordered the sequel, but then put it off, because I wanted to read it during the fall, so the vibe would be just perfect (yes, I am that extreme type of mood reader lol). <br /><br />You can guess what happened then.<br /><br />Exactly. I never picked up the sequel. <br /><br />In fact, I pretty much forgot about this series alltogether, because I discovered so many new favourites over the following months that this underrated gem got kind of pushed to the back. And there, it stayed.<br /><br />Until about a month or so ago, when I was in the process of moving and stumbled upon this book and its sequel and got flooded with beautiful, bittersweet memories, and then on a whim decided that I would finally, after all these years, continue the series.<br />But first, I had to reread book one. See if it holds up. And, admittedly, I was not just a little scared that it wouldn't. After all, my reading taste had matured quite a bit since 2016-ish, and reading the synopsis, it sounded even more cheesy than I remembered it to be.<br />I dared it though. I went to the huge, forest-like park near my new apartment where there are tiny pathways you can get lost on and little, almost-hidden stone bridges, seemingly leading into nowhere, and mysterious-looking old fountains and the most intense fall vibes you can think of, armed with a bag of cookies, my playlist of favourite autumnal emo jams and this book.<br /><br />And I devoured it. <br />It's been over 3 years, this book is still angsty as hell, and I still ate it up like chocolate.<br /><br />✉ Reasons to pick this book up despite its very bad cover and questionable blurb ✉<br /><br />This books' first couple of chapters read pretty much like every other YA paranormal romance ever. Average girls meets mysterious and Dark and brooding guy who obviously has some Dark supernatural secret, dislikes him first, then falls in love with him, then angst ensues because for some reason they absolutely CANNOT be together, yadda yadda. Sounds yawn-enducingly familiar, right? Ha. You'd THINK. <br /><br />Because pretty soon the novel makes it clear that, while it still is all of the above, it's also going places that by far exceed the realms of Twilight and suchlike, and for the longest time, the reader has no idea what these places are. Not only is the supernatural element in question something that I still consider fairly unique in comparison to other books in this genre (no vampires, no wherewolves, but something else entirely, pinky promise!), but Kelly Creagh also managed to put almost every single cliché there is in her book - and still made them not only somehow interesting, but sometimes even challenged them. Of course, now there are much better examples of trope defiance in newer YA, but everything needs a start, right? Also, I very firmly believe that all the vampire jokes in this book are definitely intentional.<br /><br />🌹<br /><br />Speaking of defiance, one thing I loved loved LOVED when I first read the book, and that still stood out to me the second time around, was the way both (!) main characters had to overcome their mutual prejudices against one another in order to get to know each other. I've always loved highschool stories of kids from different social circles teaming up and breaking the habit, of not "sticking to the status quo" (yes, that was a halfhearted High School Musical reference), and this book is a beautiful example of that.<br /><br />🌹<br /><br />You know what I also love? Enemies-to-lovers. Aaaand no instalove. And guess what? This book has that, too !! Okay, maybe it's more like mutual-dislike-to-mutual-respect-to-lovers, and their declarations of love towards the end of the book might be just a tad too dramatic to be realistic, but still. Watching them slowly open up and starting to see each other in a different light is just such a wonderful experience, especially with Varen. Also, their relationship kickstarts because they're paired together for a school project. Which is a trope I'm also such a sucker for, and I barely ever see that in a book. Instead I get love triangle and chosen ones. Why, authors, why? And can we take a moment for the fact that while there might sometimes be a certain awkwardness to some of their interactions, but it's still always sweet and genuine and, most importantly, it is never. creepy. And I very much appreciate that.<br /><br />🌹<br /><br />And then, there's, of course, the characters in general. Who are all so much more than it seems in the beginning, just like the book itself. Well, most of them.<br />There's Isobel, full of energy and determination and glorious stubbornness, who's always been goal-oriented, but who only now discovers how selfless and brave she can be. Isobel, who's definitely not the one who needs saving, but the one who saves. Despite loving the color pink! Gasp! Shock!<br />There's Varen, who's wearing his goth outfits and piercing gazes and cool sarcasm like armor, but has a mind and imagination sharp as a knife, full of phantoms and poems, and who's also heartbreakingly lonely. (Varen, who also wears a lip ring and eyeliner, which, yes, is very important to me).<br />And Gwen, my actual favourite, who's so much more than a sidekick, wearing hippie skirts and masses of bracelets before it became cool again, who's as charming as she's smart as she's loyal and who I'd honestly love to have coffee and talk schemes with. <br />There are Isobel's parents, whose actions I might not always have understood, but who are definitely not absent and clearly care about her daughter very much.<br />There are Reynolds and Pinfeathers, who are many things, and I can't put my finger on most of them, but what I can say is that I absolutely want more. Of both of them.<br />And let's not forget Danny, Isobel's 12-year-old brother, also way more than a sidekick, an icon of support and loyalty towards his sister (if he wants to be), and most definitely secretly plotting world domination.<br /><br />🌹<br /><br />Another big plus of the book, at least to me (and another thing that sets it apart from many books of that era): Instead of immediately throwing around weird and confusing worldbuilding, the book takes its time to introduce its supernatural element, and instead uses that time to focus on the characters, only to turn into a breathtaking and terrifying feverdream for the last 100-or-so pages. And while I love that part of the book, the slowly unfolding first half of it, when everything is still mysterious and new, just as the fragile, yet growing bond between Varen and Isobel, is still my favourite.<br /><br />🌹<br /><br />Aaaaand, last but not least, let's talk Poe and athmosphere !! Because Poe's work plays a massive role in this book, and while it might occasionally be a bit on the nose, I still loved all the hints and new interpretations of his works woven into the story, and of course the beautifully vivid gothic vibe it creates. Also, this book was actually the reason why I decided I wanted to read Poe, which I now have, so there were many many tiny details I didn't even notice the first time around.<br /><br />🌹<br /><br />Of course, not Everything with a capital E holds up. In fact, there where a couple of instances that most definitely turned my face into an image of confusion and irritation - here are a few examples of that:<br /><br />✉ The things that made me go ???? ✉<br /><br />🌹 Why is everything Isobel's friends say or do complete bogus ???? Like, I know this is a highschool in a YA novel from 2010 and the drama is guaranteed to be a bit over the top, but come on. They absolutely lose their shit about Varen writing his phone number on her hand (which, uhh yeah, dramatic much? but still, not necessarily something to freak out over) - because that means he's now officially stalking her/trying to murder her and that justifies literally threatening him and vandalizing his workplace ?? Mmmhh, 'kay.<br />🌹 Why, in the name of all that is good in the world, did the love interest, as much as I genuinely love his character, have to be named VAREN ???? (I mean, I get why, but that doesn't make things any better.)<br />This is a thing that genuinely didn't bother me when I first read it, but now I literally can't look at that name without having to stifle a tiny laugh of despair. <br />In case you didn't notice it yet and wonder whatever the hell I'm on about: This whole book is basically a huge reference to Poe's 'The Raven'. The love interest is named Varen.<br />Raven. Varen. Raven. Varen. Just let that sink in for a minute.<br />🌹 Why does Isobel keep trying to find excuses for Brad, when he treats her and everyone around him like shit from the start ???? And also, yes, he might not deserve to die, and yes, Isobel is a very bighearted person, but w h y is she still so hellbent on protecting him after he was the absolute worst during that porch scene (and also very much kissed her without her consent, mind you, and who knows what else if he hadn't gotten interrupted) ????<br />🌹 not necessarily a '????', but more of a trigger warning: there is also the occasional use of homophobic slurs (by Brad, of course, because who else would it be), and while it's never under a positive connotation, I think might be still good to know before going in.<br /><br />✉<br /><br />Apart from these little moments of irritation however, I still had such a good time revisiting this and relishing in the delicious angst this novel provides. And also listening to lots of AFI and MCR in the meantime (there may or may not be two very small nods to MCR in this, but my inner fangirl might as well just interpret too much into everything lol). If this sounds like something you'd vibe with, don't let the hideous cover fool you !! This book is so much more than it seems.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9097805325187370305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
